\doxysubsection{Detailed Description}
\subsubsection*{template$<$typename \+\_\+\+Scalar, int \+\_\+\+Dim, int \+\_\+\+Mode, int \+\_\+\+Options$>$\newline
class Eigen\+::\+Transform$<$ \+\_\+\+Scalar, \+\_\+\+Dim, \+\_\+\+Mode, \+\_\+\+Options $>$}
Represents an homogeneous transformation in a N dimensional space. 

\textbackslash{}geometry\+\_\+module


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em \+\_\+\+Scalar} & the scalar type, i.\+e., the type of the coefficients \\
\hline
{\em \+\_\+\+Dim} & the dimension of the space \\
\hline
{\em \+\_\+\+Mode} & the type of the transformation. Can be\+:
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item \doxylink{group__enums_ggaee59a86102f150923b0cac6d4ff05107a71e768e0581725d919d0b05f4cb83234}{Affine}\+: the transformation is stored as a (Dim+1)\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}2 matrix, where the last row is assumed to be \mbox{[}0 ... 0 1\mbox{]}.
\item \doxylink{group__enums_ggaee59a86102f150923b0cac6d4ff05107aa30a06b60d218b709020972df47de2b0}{Affine\+Compact}\+: the transformation is stored as a (Dim)x(Dim+1) matrix.
\item \doxylink{group__enums_ggaee59a86102f150923b0cac6d4ff05107aead6a2de12a17aaa4f5c523215dfccad}{Projective}\+: the transformation is stored as a (Dim+1)\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}2 matrix without any assumption.
\item \doxylink{group__enums_ggaee59a86102f150923b0cac6d4ff05107a080cd5366173608f701cd945c2335568}{Isometry}\+: same as \doxylink{group__enums_ggaee59a86102f150923b0cac6d4ff05107a71e768e0581725d919d0b05f4cb83234}{Affine} with the additional assumption that the linear part represents a rotation. This assumption is exploited to speed up some functions such as \doxylink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2plugins_2ArrayCwiseUnaryOps_8h_ab3df1b08b9c073db2a7e61a9b06bb295}{inverse()} and \doxylink{classEigen_1_1Transform_a692c68020ac2558ce87fd9dd0c7944cf}{rotation()}. 
\end{DoxyItemize}\\
\hline
{\em \+\_\+\+Options} & has the same meaning as in class \doxylink{classEigen_1_1Matrix}{Matrix}. It allows to specify Dont\+Align and/or Row\+Major. These Options are passed directly to the underlying matrix type.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}
The homography is internally represented and stored by a matrix which is available through the \doxylink{classEigen_1_1Transform_a146347395d7dcfd250b6f9f96f9ed233}{matrix()} method. To understand the behavior of this class you have to think a \doxylink{classEigen_1_1Transform}{Transform} object as its internal matrix representation. The chosen convention is right multiply\+:


\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceabsl_a828e0f13fb3947cdf6406b7a4feec8aca9e3669d19b675bd57058fd4664205d2a}{v}}\textcolor{stringliteral}{'\ =\ T\ *\ v\ }}

\end{DoxyCode}


Therefore, an affine transformation matrix M is shaped like this\+:

$ \left( \begin{array}{cc}
 linear & translation\\
 0 ... 0 & 1
 \end{array} \right) $

Note that for a projective transformation the last row can be anything, and then the interpretation of different parts might be slightly different.

However, unlike a plain matrix, the \doxylink{classEigen_1_1Transform}{Transform} class provides many features simplifying both its assembly and usage. In particular, it can be composed with any other transformations (\doxylink{classEigen_1_1Transform}{Transform},\doxylink{classEigen_1_1Translation}{Translation},\doxylink{classEigen_1_1RotationBase}{Rotation\+Base},\doxylink{classEigen_1_1DiagonalMatrix}{Diagonal\+Matrix}) and can be directly used to transform implicit homogeneous vectors. All these operations are handled via the operator\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}. For the composition of transformations, its principle consists to first convert the right/left hand sides of the product to a compatible (Dim+1)\texorpdfstring{$^\wedge$}{\string^}2 matrix and then perform a pure matrix product. Of course, internally, operator\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} tries to perform the minimal number of operations according to the nature of each terms. Likewise, when applying the transform to points, the latters are automatically promoted to homogeneous vectors before doing the matrix product. The conventions to homogeneous representations are performed as follow\+:

{\bfseries{\doxylink{classEigen_1_1Translation}{Translation}}} t (Dim)x(1)\+:    $ \left( \begin{array}{cc}
 I & t \\
 0\,...\,0 & 1
 \end{array} \right) $

{\bfseries{Rotation}} R (Dim)x(\+Dim)\+:    $ \left( \begin{array}{cc}
 R & 0\\
 0\,...\,0 & 1
 \end{array} \right) $             {\bfseries{Scaling}} {\bfseries{\doxylink{classEigen_1_1DiagonalMatrix}{Diagonal\+Matrix}}} S (Dim)x(\+Dim)\+:    $ \left( \begin{array}{cc}
 S & 0\\
 0\,...\,0 & 1
 \end{array} \right) $

{\bfseries{Column}} {\bfseries{point}} v (Dim)x(1)\+:    $ \left( \begin{array}{c}
 v\\
 1
 \end{array} \right) $

{\bfseries{Set}} {\bfseries{of}} {\bfseries{column}} {\bfseries{points}} V1...Vn (Dim)x(n)\+:    $ \left( \begin{array}{ccc}
 v_1 & ... & v_n\\
 1 & ... & 1
 \end{array} \right) $

The concatenation of a \doxylink{classEigen_1_1Transform}{Transform} object with any kind of other transformation always returns a \doxylink{classEigen_1_1Transform}{Transform} object.

A little exception to the "{}as pure matrix product"{} rule is the case of the transformation of non homogeneous vectors by an affine transformation. In that case the last matrix row can be ignored, and the product returns non homogeneous vectors.

Since, for instance, a Dim x Dim matrix is interpreted as a linear transformation, it is not possible to directly transform Dim vectors stored in a Dim x Dim matrix. The solution is either to use a Dim x Dynamic matrix or explicitly request a vector transformation by making the vector homogeneous\+: 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{m\textcolor{stringliteral}{'\ =\ T\ *\ m.colwise().homogeneous();}}

\end{DoxyCode}
 Note that there is zero overhead.

Conversion methods from/to Qt\textquotesingle{}s QMatrix and QTransform are available if the preprocessor token EIGEN\+\_\+\+QT\+\_\+\+SUPPORT is defined.

This class can be extended with the help of the plugin mechanism described on the page Topic\+Customizing\+\_\+\+Plugins by defining the preprocessor symbol {\ttfamily EIGEN\+\_\+\+TRANSFORM\+\_\+\+PLUGIN}.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
class \doxylink{classEigen_1_1Matrix}{Matrix}, class \doxylink{classEigen_1_1Quaternion}{Quaternion} 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

template$<$typename Rotation\+Matrix\+Type , typename Scaling\+Matrix\+Type $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} void \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Transform}{Eigen\+::\+Transform}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Transform_a4e69ced9d651745b8ed4eda46f41795d}{Scalar}}, Dim, Mode, Options $>$\+::compute\+Rotation\+Scaling (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{Rotation\+Matrix\+Type \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{rotation}{, }\item[{Scaling\+Matrix\+Type \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{scaling}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const}

decomposes the linear part of the transformation as a product rotation x scaling, the scaling being not necessarily positive.

If either pointer is zero, the corresponding computation is skipped.

\Hypertarget{classEigen_1_1Transform_a20ca137b84f18b9c41a0fef9c222e0da}\index{Eigen::Transform$<$ \_Scalar, \_Dim, \_Mode, \_Options $>$@{Eigen::Transform$<$ \_Scalar, \_Dim, \_Mode, \_Options $>$}!inverse@{inverse}}
\index{inverse@{inverse}!Eigen::Transform$<$ \_Scalar, \_Dim, \_Mode, \_Options $>$@{Eigen::Transform$<$ \_Scalar, \_Dim, \_Mode, \_Options $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{inverse()}{inverse()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1Transform_a20ca137b84f18b9c41a0fef9c222e0da} 
template$<$typename \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Transform_a4e69ced9d651745b8ed4eda46f41795d}{Scalar}} , int Dim, int Mode, int Options$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Transform}{Transform}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Transform_a4e69ced9d651745b8ed4eda46f41795d}{Scalar}}, Dim, Mode, Options $>$ \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Transform}{Eigen\+::\+Transform}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Transform_a4e69ced9d651745b8ed4eda46f41795d}{Scalar}}, Dim, Mode, Options $>$\+::inverse (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{group__enums_gaee59a86102f150923b0cac6d4ff05107}{Transform\+Traits}}}]{hint}{ = {\ttfamily (\mbox{\hyperlink{group__enums_gaee59a86102f150923b0cac6d4ff05107}{Transform\+Traits}})Mode}}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
the inverse transformation according to some given knowledge on {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this}.
\end{DoxyReturn}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em hint} & allows to optimize the inversion process when the transformation is known to be not a general transformation (optional). The possible values are\+:
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item \doxylink{group__enums_ggaee59a86102f150923b0cac6d4ff05107aead6a2de12a17aaa4f5c523215dfccad}{Projective} if the transformation is not necessarily affine, i.\+e., if the last row is not guaranteed to be \mbox{[}0 ... 0 1\mbox{]}
\item \doxylink{group__enums_ggaee59a86102f150923b0cac6d4ff05107a71e768e0581725d919d0b05f4cb83234}{Affine} if the last row can be assumed to be \mbox{[}0 ... 0 1\mbox{]}
\item \doxylink{group__enums_ggaee59a86102f150923b0cac6d4ff05107a080cd5366173608f701cd945c2335568}{Isometry} if the transformation is only a concatenations of translations and rotations. The default is the template class parameter {\ttfamily Mode}.
\end{DoxyItemize}\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
unless {\itshape traits} is always set to No\+Shear or No\+Scaling, this function requires the generic inverse method of \doxylink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase}{Matrix\+Base} defined in the LU module. If you forget to include this module, then you will get hard to debug linking errors.
\end{DoxyWarning}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\doxylink{classEigen_1_1MatrixBase_add090d35d12d42d01eba1a24f22cf8f3}{Matrix\+Base\+::inverse()} 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\end{center}
\end{figure}

\index{inverse@{inverse}!Eigen::Transform$<$ \_Scalar, \_Dim, \_Mode, \_Options $>$@{Eigen::Transform$<$ \_Scalar, \_Dim, \_Mode, \_Options $>$}}

template$<$typename \+\_\+\+Scalar , int \+\_\+\+Dim, int \+\_\+\+Mode, int \+\_\+\+Options$>$ \\
template$<$typename Diagonal\+Derived $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Transform_ae00e920cba80994315dc0b6ad152ea13}{Transform\+Time\+Diagonal\+Return\+Type}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Transform}{Eigen\+::\+Transform}}$<$ \+\_\+\+Scalar, \+\_\+\+Dim, \+\_\+\+Mode, \+\_\+\+Options $>$\+::operator\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1DiagonalBase}{Diagonal\+Base}}$<$ Diagonal\+Derived $>$ \&}]{b}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
The product expression of a transform {\itshape a} times a diagonal matrix {\itshape b} 
\end{DoxyReturn}
The rhs diagonal matrix is interpreted as an affine scaling transformation. The product results in a \doxylink{classEigen_1_1Transform}{Transform} of the same type (mode) as the lhs only if the lhs mode is no isometry. In that case, the returned transform is an affinity. \Hypertarget{classEigen_1_1Transform_a56eb11fd16b64878e3e07681ab7a695d}\index{Eigen::Transform$<$ \_Scalar, \_Dim, \_Mode, \_Options $>$@{Eigen::Transform$<$ \_Scalar, \_Dim, \_Mode, \_Options $>$}!operator\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}@{operator\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}}
\index{operator\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}@{operator\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}!Eigen::Transform$<$ \_Scalar, \_Dim, \_Mode, \_Options $>$@{Eigen::Transform$<$ \_Scalar, \_Dim, \_Mode, \_Options $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{operator\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}()}{operator*()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [3/15]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1Transform_a56eb11fd16b64878e3e07681ab7a695d} 
template$<$typename \+\_\+\+Scalar , int \+\_\+\+Dim, int \+\_\+\+Mode, int \+\_\+\+Options$>$ \\
template$<$typename Other\+Derived $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} \mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_af2b60117c00a6e75812de43bfe7db3b1}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+STRONG\+\_\+\+INLINE}} const \mbox{\hyperlink{structEigen_1_1internal_1_1transform__right__product__impl}{internal\+::transform\+\_\+right\+\_\+product\+\_\+impl}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Transform}{Transform}}, Other\+Derived $>$\+::\+Result\+Type \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Transform}{Eigen\+::\+Transform}}$<$ \+\_\+\+Scalar, \+\_\+\+Dim, \+\_\+\+Mode, \+\_\+\+Options $>$\+::operator\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{structEigen_1_1EigenBase}{Eigen\+Base}}$<$ Other\+Derived $>$ \&}]{other}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the product between the transform {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this} and a matrix expression {\itshape other}.
\end{DoxyReturn}
The right-\/hand-\/side {\itshape other} can be either\+: \begin{DoxyItemize}
\item an homogeneous vector of size Dim+1, \item a set of homogeneous vectors of size Dim+1 x N, \item a transformation matrix of size Dim+1 x Dim+1.\end{DoxyItemize}
Moreover, if {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this} represents an affine transformation (i.\+e., Mode!=Projective), then {\itshape other} can also be\+: \begin{DoxyItemize}
\item a point of size Dim (computes\+: 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{this-\/>\mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Transform_a535bd63d047c2a36585c3f9b62219a1e}{linear}}()\ *\ other\ +\ this-\/>\mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Transform_afa93ba97d26912bb3d8777cbed102045}{translation}}()}

\end{DoxyCode}
), \item a set of N points as a Dim x N matrix (computes\+: 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{(this-\/>\mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Transform_a535bd63d047c2a36585c3f9b62219a1e}{linear}}()\ *\ other).colwise()\ +\ this-\/>\mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Transform_afa93ba97d26912bb3d8777cbed102045}{translation}}()}

\end{DoxyCode}
),\end{DoxyItemize}
In all cases, the return type is a matrix or vector of same sizes as the right-\/hand-\/side {\itshape other}.

If you want to interpret {\itshape other} as a linear or affine transformation, then first convert it to a Transform$<$$>$ type, or do your own cooking.

Finally, if you want to apply Affine transformations to vectors, then explicitly apply the linear part only\+: 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{\mbox{\hyperlink{group__Geometry__Module_ga17e901de8ff882aea7845c5457db6a4f}{Affine3f}}\ \mbox{\hyperlink{abseil-cpp_2absl_2base_2internal_2fast__type__id__test_8cc_a1ea955b94ea8dc35e689055712257459}{A}};}
\DoxyCodeLine{Vector3f\ \mbox{\hyperlink{abseil-cpp_2absl_2container_2flat__hash__map__test_8cc_ac3f9ff4294615df8b7e9684b7d6fddc7}{v1}},\ \mbox{\hyperlink{abseil-cpp_2absl_2container_2flat__hash__map__test_8cc_aa517e2fff4a8c9cba11391ca12f91803}{v2}};}
\DoxyCodeLine{\mbox{\hyperlink{abseil-cpp_2absl_2container_2flat__hash__map__test_8cc_aa517e2fff4a8c9cba11391ca12f91803}{v2}}\ =\ A.linear()\ *\ \mbox{\hyperlink{abseil-cpp_2absl_2container_2flat__hash__map__test_8cc_ac3f9ff4294615df8b7e9684b7d6fddc7}{v1}};}

\end{DoxyCode}

template$<$typename \+\_\+\+Scalar , int \+\_\+\+Dim, int \+\_\+\+Mode, int \+\_\+\+Options$>$ \\
template$<$typename Other\+Derived $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} \mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_af2b60117c00a6e75812de43bfe7db3b1}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+STRONG\+\_\+\+INLINE}} const \mbox{\hyperlink{structEigen_1_1internal_1_1transform__right__product__impl}{internal\+::transform\+\_\+right\+\_\+product\+\_\+impl}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Transform}{Transform}}, Other\+Derived $>$\+::\+Result\+Type \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Transform}{Eigen\+::\+Transform}}$<$ \+\_\+\+Scalar, \+\_\+\+Dim, \+\_\+\+Mode, \+\_\+\+Options $>$\+::operator\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{structEigen_1_1EigenBase}{Eigen\+Base}}$<$ Other\+Derived $>$ \&}]{other}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
an expression of the product between the transform {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this} and a matrix expression {\itshape other}.
\end{DoxyReturn}
The right-\/hand-\/side {\itshape other} can be either\+: \begin{DoxyItemize}
\item an homogeneous vector of size Dim+1, \item a set of homogeneous vectors of size Dim+1 x N, \item a transformation matrix of size Dim+1 x Dim+1.\end{DoxyItemize}
Moreover, if {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this} represents an affine transformation (i.\+e., Mode!=Projective), then {\itshape other} can also be\+: \begin{DoxyItemize}
\item a point of size Dim (computes\+: 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{this-\/>\mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Transform_a535bd63d047c2a36585c3f9b62219a1e}{linear}}()\ *\ other\ +\ this-\/>\mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Transform_afa93ba97d26912bb3d8777cbed102045}{translation}}()}

\end{DoxyCode}
), \item a set of N points as a Dim x N matrix (computes\+: 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{(this-\/>\mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Transform_a535bd63d047c2a36585c3f9b62219a1e}{linear}}()\ *\ other).colwise()\ +\ this-\/>\mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Transform_afa93ba97d26912bb3d8777cbed102045}{translation}}()}

\end{DoxyCode}
),\end{DoxyItemize}
In all cases, the return type is a matrix or vector of same sizes as the right-\/hand-\/side {\itshape other}.

If you want to interpret {\itshape other} as a linear or affine transformation, then first convert it to a Transform$<$$>$ type, or do your own cooking.

Finally, if you want to apply Affine transformations to vectors, then explicitly apply the linear part only\+: 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{\mbox{\hyperlink{group__Geometry__Module_ga17e901de8ff882aea7845c5457db6a4f}{Affine3f}}\ \mbox{\hyperlink{abseil-cpp_2absl_2base_2internal_2fast__type__id__test_8cc_a1ea955b94ea8dc35e689055712257459}{A}};}
\DoxyCodeLine{Vector3f\ \mbox{\hyperlink{abseil-cpp_2absl_2container_2flat__hash__map__test_8cc_ac3f9ff4294615df8b7e9684b7d6fddc7}{v1}},\ \mbox{\hyperlink{abseil-cpp_2absl_2container_2flat__hash__map__test_8cc_aa517e2fff4a8c9cba11391ca12f91803}{v2}};}
\DoxyCodeLine{\mbox{\hyperlink{abseil-cpp_2absl_2container_2flat__hash__map__test_8cc_aa517e2fff4a8c9cba11391ca12f91803}{v2}}\ =\ A.linear()\ *\ \mbox{\hyperlink{abseil-cpp_2absl_2container_2flat__hash__map__test_8cc_ac3f9ff4294615df8b7e9684b7d6fddc7}{v1}};}

\end{DoxyCode}

\Hypertarget{classEigen_1_1Transform_a6cfe95a4da33cfbc2092ac2fedee332f}\index{Eigen::Transform$<$ \_Scalar, \_Dim, \_Mode, \_Options $>$@{Eigen::Transform$<$ \_Scalar, \_Dim, \_Mode, \_Options $>$}!rotate@{rotate}}
\index{rotate@{rotate}!Eigen::Transform$<$ \_Scalar, \_Dim, \_Mode, \_Options $>$@{Eigen::Transform$<$ \_Scalar, \_Dim, \_Mode, \_Options $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rotate()}{rotate()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [2/3]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1Transform_a6cfe95a4da33cfbc2092ac2fedee332f} 
template$<$typename \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Transform_a4e69ced9d651745b8ed4eda46f41795d}{Scalar}} , int Dim, int Mode, int Options$>$ \\
template$<$typename Rotation\+Type $>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Transform}{Transform}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Transform_a4e69ced9d651745b8ed4eda46f41795d}{Scalar}}, Dim, Mode, Options $>$ \& \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Transform}{Eigen\+::\+Transform}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Transform_a4e69ced9d651745b8ed4eda46f41795d}{Scalar}}, Dim, Mode, Options $>$\+::rotate (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const Rotation\+Type \&}]{rotation}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Applies on the right the rotation represented by the rotation {\itshape rotation} to {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this} and returns a reference to {\ttfamily \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}this}.

The template parameter {\itshape Rotation\+Type} is the type of the rotation which must be known by \doxylink{namespaceEigen_1_1internal_ac38f2eb8d2f6922edaa5c3f9d99f3673}{internal\+::to\+Rotation\+Matrix$<$$>$}.

Natively supported types includes\+:
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item any scalar (2D),
\item a Dim x Dim matrix expression,
\item a \doxylink{classEigen_1_1Quaternion}{Quaternion} (3D),
\item a \doxylink{classEigen_1_1AngleAxis}{Angle\+Axis} (3D)
\end{DoxyItemize}

This mechanism is easily extendable to support user types such as Euler angles, or a pair of \doxylink{classEigen_1_1Quaternion}{Quaternion} for 4D rotations.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
rotate(\+Scalar), class \doxylink{classEigen_1_1Quaternion}{Quaternion}, class \doxylink{classEigen_1_1AngleAxis}{Angle\+Axis}, prerotate(\+Rotation\+Type) 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\Hypertarget{classEigen_1_1Transform_a692c68020ac2558ce87fd9dd0c7944cf}\index{Eigen::Transform$<$ \_Scalar, \_Dim, \_Mode, \_Options $>$@{Eigen::Transform$<$ \_Scalar, \_Dim, \_Mode, \_Options $>$}!rotation@{rotation}}
\index{rotation@{rotation}!Eigen::Transform$<$ \_Scalar, \_Dim, \_Mode, \_Options $>$@{Eigen::Transform$<$ \_Scalar, \_Dim, \_Mode, \_Options $>$}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rotation()}{rotation()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classEigen_1_1Transform_a692c68020ac2558ce87fd9dd0c7944cf} 
template$<$typename \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Transform_a4e69ced9d651745b8ed4eda46f41795d}{Scalar}} , int Dim, int Mode, int Options$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Transform}{Transform}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Transform_a4e69ced9d651745b8ed4eda46f41795d}{Scalar}}, Dim, Mode, Options $>$\mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Transform_ae7e06e9c5b30e33220efb86e88db2a2c}{\+::\+Rotation\+Return\+Type}} \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Transform}{Eigen\+::\+Transform}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Transform_a4e69ced9d651745b8ed4eda46f41795d}{Scalar}}, Dim, Mode, Options $>$\+::rotation (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
the rotation part of the transformation
\end{DoxyReturn}
If Mode==Isometry, then this method is an alias for \doxylink{classEigen_1_1Transform_a535bd63d047c2a36585c3f9b62219a1e}{linear()}, otherwise it calls \doxylink{classEigen_1_1Transform_aff2a75622ed0a24dbe4bd22e5aeccb78}{compute\+Rotation\+Scaling()} to extract the rotation through a SVD decomposition.

\textbackslash{}svd\+\_\+module

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
The product expression of a diagonal matrix {\itshape a} times a transform {\itshape b} 
\end{DoxyReturn}
The lhs diagonal matrix is interpreted as an affine scaling transformation. The product results in a \doxylink{classEigen_1_1Transform}{Transform} of the same type (mode) as the lhs only if the lhs mode is no isometry. In that case, the returned transform is an affinity. \Hypertarget{classEigen_1_1Transform_a1ee8a506136a4ac8084b2913cc249ec8}\index{Eigen::Transform$<$ \_Scalar, \_Dim, \_Mode, \_Options $>$@{Eigen::Transform$<$ \_Scalar, \_Dim, \_Mode, \_Options $>$}!operator\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}@{operator\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
The product expression of a diagonal matrix {\itshape a} times a transform {\itshape b} 
\end{DoxyReturn}
The lhs diagonal matrix is interpreted as an affine scaling transformation. The product results in a \doxylink{classEigen_1_1Transform}{Transform} of the same type (mode) as the lhs only if the lhs mode is no isometry. In that case, the returned transform is an affinity. \Hypertarget{classEigen_1_1Transform_acf92e7145cc20f09f5d0bee9fce26389}\index{Eigen::Transform$<$ \_Scalar, \_Dim, \_Mode, \_Options $>$@{Eigen::Transform$<$ \_Scalar, \_Dim, \_Mode, \_Options $>$}!operator\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}@{operator\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
the product expression of a transformation matrix {\itshape a} times a transform {\itshape b} 
\end{DoxyReturn}
The left hand side {\itshape other} can be either\+: \begin{DoxyItemize}
\item a linear transformation matrix of size Dim x Dim, \item an affine transformation matrix of size Dim x Dim+1, \item a general transformation matrix of size Dim+1 x Dim+1. \end{DoxyItemize}

\mbox{\hyperlink{eigen_2Eigen_2src_2Core_2util_2Macros_8h_a9efec3cfd22b9a33bead9c6718d128da}{EIGEN\+\_\+\+DEVICE\+\_\+\+FUNC}} const \mbox{\hyperlink{structEigen_1_1internal_1_1transform__left__product__impl}{internal\+::transform\+\_\+left\+\_\+product\+\_\+impl}}$<$ Other\+Derived, Mode, Options, \+\_\+\+Dim, \+\_\+\+Dim+1 $>$\+::\+Result\+Type operator\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{structEigen_1_1EigenBase}{Eigen\+Base}}$<$ Other\+Derived $>$ \&}]{a}{, }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{classEigen_1_1Transform}{Transform}}$<$ \+\_\+\+Scalar, \+\_\+\+Dim, \+\_\+\+Mode, \+\_\+\+Options $>$ \&}]{b}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [friend]}}

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
the product expression of a transformation matrix {\itshape a} times a transform {\itshape b} 
\end{DoxyReturn}
The left hand side {\itshape other} can be either\+: \begin{DoxyItemize}
\item a linear transformation matrix of size Dim x Dim, \item an affine transformation matrix of size Dim x Dim+1, \item a general transformation matrix of size Dim+1 x Dim+1. \end{DoxyItemize}
